  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer972911680834269054">"El laberinto de los espíritus", es el desenlace de la saga de "El cementerio de los libros olvidados" que se inició en 2001 con "La sombra del viento" y continuó en 2008 con "El juego del ángel" y en 2011 con "El prisionero del cielo".<br/><br/>Elevadas por la crítica internacional a la categoría de clásico contemporáneo, las novelas de "El cementerio de los libros olvidados" se ha</span>
  <span id="freeText972911680834269054" style="display:none">"El laberinto de los espíritus", es el desenlace de la saga de "El cementerio de los libros olvidados" que se inició en 2001 con "La sombra del viento" y continuó en 2008 con "El juego del ángel" y en 2011 con "El prisionero del cielo".<br /><br />Elevadas por la crítica internacional a la categoría de clásico contemporáneo, las novelas de "El cementerio de los libros olvidados" se han convertido en uno de los universos literarios más apasionantes del nuevo siglo, y Carlos Ruiz Zafón en el escritor español más leído en todo el mundo después de Cervantes.</span>

I decided to enjoy the tale as a tale and make the corrections in my mind. The story is great but Zafón could did a better job in the timeline.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_more_filters_span_tip_182').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2446041642" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2446041642" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2446041642?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781982553388" href="/book/show/40399602-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2446041642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5578372576118142121">The gothic universe created in The Shadow of the Wind, and the following alleyways forged in the sequels culminate in this finale, where all the threads connect to illuminate the horrors, secrets, and terrors of the harrowing and heartbreaking years of the Spanish Civil War and Franco's dictatorship that overturned democratic rule, aided and abetted by the Catholic Church. I loved The Shadow of the Wind and the universe it established with The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, but the following two b</span>
  <span id="freeText5578372576118142121" style="display:none">The gothic universe created in The Shadow of the Wind, and the following alleyways forged in the sequels culminate in this finale, where all the threads connect to illuminate the horrors, secrets, and terrors of the harrowing and heartbreaking years of the Spanish Civil War and Franco's dictatorship that overturned democratic rule, aided and abetted by the Catholic Church. I loved The Shadow of the Wind and the universe it established with The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, but the following two books, I was disappointed in, I liked them but they fell far short when it came to emulating the brilliance of the first. Mostly, I loved this, it's atmospheric with its beautiful prose, Zafon expertly constructs the labyrinth of secrets, the magic of books, with its intrigue, friendship, love and family. However, if I am to be honest, there is an unevenness to the narrative, and the last part of the book, in my eyes, is the weakest. We are introduced to the seductive and enigmatic 29 year old Alicia Gris, losing her parents in the relentless bombing of Barcelona in 1938 by the fascists, left with injuries and pain that is to affect her mobility for life. For over a decade, Alicia has worked for Leandro and the political police in Madrid. She wants out, but has to take on one last assignment, find Culture Minister, Mauricio Valls, who has disappeared, along with his driver, presumed kidnapped by enemies.<br /><br />Valls was the governor of Montjuic prison, where a number of writers were imprisoned, including David Martin and Victor Mataix, the writer of The Labyrinth of the Spirits, a take on Alice in Wonderland for his daughter, but where the heroine, Ariadna, descends into Barcelona's underworld to encounter horror after horror, imagined out of Spain's actual realities of that period. Torture and murder were the norm in the prison, and strangely, Valls had a copy of an edition of Mataix's banned novel which he was perusing. Alicia cottons on that her assignment is not what it purports to be, and she, along with others face deadly dangers by those who have a vested interest in ensuring the dark deeds, secrets and corruption of the fascist regime remain buried. Spain, Barcelona, The City of the Damned, steeped in the blood letting, with its proliferation of secret police, the widespread fear of the likes of Major Fumero and the good looking but monstrous Hendaya, is a place where lies and fiction have the greatest agency, and the truth is to be doubted and ruthlessly suppressed.<br /><br />The Sempere family with its secrets and bookshop return, with Daniel harbouring bitter consuming thoughts of revenge for what happened to Isabella, his mother. Fermin, comic, saviour and philosopher, and the unwavering and resolute Alicia were my favourite characters, both connected to each other and the Semperes. The love of books, the joys of reading are central to Zafon's quartet of novels, as indeed is writing, the need to throw light on the darkest of shadows of Franco's fascist regime with his inner cabal and acolytes, defined by their kleptocracy, butchery, corruption, murdering en masse with impunity, and their avarice. The gloom of Barcelona begins to lift with Franco's death, and chinks of light begin to filter through as slow faltering steps take place as Spain begins to move on from its nightmarish history. Overall, this is bewitching and beguiling storytelling documenting the unbearable, emotionally heartbreaking inhumanity of Spain's fascist past which I must recommend highly, despite its imperfections. Many thanks to Orion for an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5578372576118142121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3219079978" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3219079978" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3219079978?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781474606219" href="/book/show/52036183-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=masterpieces">masterpieces</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3219079978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14916256036334862391"><b>An absorbing literary masterpiece embedded with every range of emotions.<br/><br/><i><blockquote>“Tell our stories to the world, and never forget that we exist so long as someone remembers us.” </blockquote></i></b><br/><br/>To express how much I loved <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i>, and the entirety of <i>The Cemetery of the Forgotten Books</i>, is a challenging task that I never predicted would ever happen to me, but attempt it I shall. I think it’s a seriously missed but redeemable opportunity that many readers didn’t continue reading the series after they</span>
  <span id="freeText14916256036334862391" style="display:none"><b>An absorbing literary masterpiece embedded with every range of emotions.<br><br><i><blockquote>“Tell our stories to the world, and never forget that we exist so long as someone remembers us.” </blockquote></i></b><br><br>To express how much I loved <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i>, and the entirety of <i>The Cemetery of the Forgotten Books</i>, is a challenging task that I never predicted would ever happen to me, but attempt it I shall. I think it’s a seriously missed but redeemable opportunity that many readers didn’t continue reading the series after they finished <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>. For the sake of comparison, there are more than 436k ratings for The <i>Shadow of the Wind</i> on Goodreads at the time of writing this review, <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> has 22k ratings. Don’t get me wrong, <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> is an incredible book that worked great as a standalone; I won’t deny that. However, believe me when I say that there’s more—so much more—to the astonishing tales you’ve read in <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>. If you truly want to experience the full magnitude of Zafón’s astounding talent as a master storyteller, and I can’t emphasize this highly enough, it is mandatory for you to read all four books in this series. <br><br><b>Picture: <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits VII: Ariadna and The Scarlet Prince</i> by Vincent Chong</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591358756i/29598392._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> is the fourth and final volume in <i>The Cemetery of Forgotten Books</i> series by Carlos Ruiz Zafón. I can only speak from my own experience, although it has been stated that you can begin your journey through this series from whichever installment, I strongly suggest you read it in publication order. I personally believe that the key points, characterizations, and revelations would work so much better this way. The story in <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> mostly follows the tale of Alicia Gris, at least for the first half, as she tries to unravel the most shocking conspiracies in the history of Spain. I was surprised by this at first, but knowing Zafón, I immediately knew there was no need to worry; nothing he writes in this quartet was ever redundant, everything is always important. <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> is the biggest book in the series, and Zafón had time to build and develop a new story—that’s how it seemed at first anyway—and characters from scratch before connecting all the dots that shaped the tapestry of tragedy, regrets, ambition, and love. It is a bittersweet tale that utilizes everything established in the previous three books; stories within stories, passion for books, reading, writing, and many more, eventually ending these extraordinary stories with an extremely satisfying conclusion.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “You’d be surprised at how often one looks in the present or in the future for answers that are always in the past.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><i>The Cemetery of Forgotten Books</i> is a series filled with well-written characters that are deeply flawed and complex. Daniel Sempere, Fermin, Bea, David Martin, Alicia Gris, many more characters I refrain from mentioning to avoid spoilers, and I’m happy to say that their respective stories reached a proper closure here. All of the characters throughout the series, one way or another, played an irreplaceable role in this maze of lives and destiny. The characters have become so real to me that the appearances/mentioning of their names sparked invoked a reaction; I was scared for them, I cared about their journey, and during their pursuits of better lives and truths, the heartbreaking revelations they stumbled upon… hurts. When the memories buried under mountains of silence resurface and act as a harbinger of pain instead of light, my heart actually broke together with the characters; I was stunned.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Nobody must know what I have explained here. Nobody must know the truth, because I’ve learned that in this world truth only hurts, and God loves and helps those who lie.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>That’s how engrossed I was by the stories and characters that Zafón has crafted throughout this novel and quartet. These broken souls have gone through many gangrenes of hope, and I genuinely want them to find happiness. Whether they truly find happiness or not, you should read the series and find out for yourself.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Sometimes, when the gods aren’t looking and destiny loses its way, even good people get a taste of good luck in their lives.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>There isn’t much more I can say regarding the magnificence of this novel without elaborating upon spoilery details, and I don’t want that; I want you to be surprised and amazed by Zafón’s masterful storytelling just like I did. However, allow me one more opportunity to praise Zafón and Lucia Graves’ translation. As always, the prose was utterly unputdownable, atmospheric, immersive, and evocative. For the first time in the series, Zafón uses both third-person and first-person narration told from the perspective of multiple characters, and this helps demonstrates the complexity and astounding accomplishment that Zafón has achieved with his large-scale stories. Juggling and showing events from multiple characters instead of just one this time definitely boost the strengths of the narrative immeasurably. I found Zafon’s prose to be highly relatable, and as always, there were a myriad of quotes I highlighted throughout the novel that I wish I can share with you. Unfortunately, I can’t; the quantity would require a section of its own.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“A painting is never finished. The trick is to know at what point to leave it unfinished.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b>Picture: <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> by Vincent Chong</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591358756i/29598393._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have traversed through these labyrinths of stories, and I will conclude by saying that I loved this finale even more than the critically acclaimed <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>. This novel is a brilliant masterwork that every reader must read; Zafón has concluded <i>The Cemetery of Forgotten Books</i> terrifically. I’ll even go as far as claiming that <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> is my number one favorite non-SFF novel at the moment. The gigantic puzzle constructed by words throughout the series has reached its spellbinding completion. Thrilling mystery, compelling narrative, endearing characters, and engaging prose have been demonstrated effortlessly. Not a single page of this 800 pages novel was dull to me, and I feel both satisfied and sorrowful that the time of farewell is here. Goodbye for now The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, I’m confident we’ll meet again. <br><br>Thank you to Lucia Graves for the superb English translation, and most of all, thank you to Carlos Ruiz Zafón for writing such an outstanding series.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Stories have no beginning and no end, only doors through which one may enter them. <br>A story is an endless labyrinth of words, images, and spirits, conjured up to show us the invisible truth about ourselves. A story is, after all, a conversation between the narrator and the reader, and just as narrators can only relate as far as their ability will permit, so too readers can only read as far as what is already written in their souls.<br>This is the golden rule that sustains every artifice of paper and ink. Because when the lights go out, when the music ends and the stalls are empty again, the only thing that matters is the mirage that has been engraved in the theater of the imagination all readers hold in their mind. This, and the hope every maker of tales carries within: that readers will open their hearts to these little creatures made of ink and paper, and give them a part of themselves so they can be immortal, even if only for a few minutes.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Series Review:</u>
  </i>
</b><br><br><i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> = <u>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3219069668?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">4.5/5 stars</a>
  </b>
</u><br><i>The Angel's Game</i> = <u>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3219075086?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">4.5/5 stars</a>
  </b>
</u><br><i>The Prisoner of Heaven</i> = <u>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3219077742?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">4.5/5 stars</a>
  </b>
</u><br><i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> = <b>
  <u>5/5 stars</u>
</b><br><br><i>The Cemetery of Forgotten Books</i> = <b>
  <u>18.5/20 stars</u>
</b><br><br><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780062668707/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br><br><b>You can find <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2020/06/05/book-review-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits-the-cemetery-of-forgotten-books-4-by-carlos-ruiz-zafon/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u> and the rest of my reviews at <u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b><br><br><i>Special thanks to my Patrons on <b><u><a href="https://www.patreon.com/petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Patreon</a></u></b> for giving me extra support towards my passion for reading and reviewing!<br><br>My Patrons: Alfred, Devin, Hamad, Jimmy Nutts, Joie, Mike, Miracle, Nicholas.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14916256036334862391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2374357672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2374357672" />
    <a title="Lucy Langford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford"><img alt="Lucy Langford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518091381p2/74034800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2374357672?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Langford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Langford" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford">Lucy Langford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781474606189" href="/book/show/39099067-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2374357672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11995710841166450195">4.5****<br/><i>The hope every maker of tales carries within: that readers will open their hearts to these little creatures made of ink and paper, and give them a part of themselves so they can be immortal, even if only for a few minutes.</i><br/><br/>An absolutely amazing and spellbinding book to finish off the "Shadow of the Wind" quartet. This book draws on old characters and new, strung together into a intricate interconnected web of a plot that had me absolutely gripped. We get to see the beloved Barcelona in all</span>
  <span id="freeText11995710841166450195" style="display:none">4.5****<br /><i>The hope every maker of tales carries within: that readers will open their hearts to these little creatures made of ink and paper, and give them a part of themselves so they can be immortal, even if only for a few minutes.</i><br /><br />An absolutely amazing and spellbinding book to finish off the "Shadow of the Wind" quartet. This book draws on old characters and new, strung together into a intricate interconnected web of a plot that had me absolutely gripped. We get to see the beloved Barcelona in all its glory and walk the streets with mystery and political intrigue and espionage.<br /><br />This book starts with the disappearance of Mauricio Valls, a prominent figure from previous books, who overlooked Montjuic Castle where numerous people "disappeared" and were tortured and killed. Sent to find Valls, this book introduces the alluring Alicia Gris whose last assignment it is is to find Valls so that she can then be granted utter freedom from working as an investigator. From this investigation Alicia is introduced to new mysteries and secrets and questioning who she can trust. Alicia Gris has the stand offish personality and a secret dark past rivaling that of Lisbeth Salander, but also has the brave and brash actions and inquisitiveness of Clarice Starling; she has easily become one of my favourite investigators in a novel. Through this novel she is entangled with the Sempere family and its secrets, as well as being placed into the illusive and shadowy literary labyrinth, including that of the seemingly magical 'Cemetery of Forgotten Books.' <br /><br />Carlos Ruiz Zafon writes with such beauty and descriptiveness, mirroring that of the first book "The Shadow of the Wind". Although this was a large book , Zafon’s writing had me completely ensnared in the plot that I only put it down when I felt too tired. He brings both beauty and humour, as well as tragedy to his writing.<br /><br />The great thing about Zafon’s books is that you do not need to read the previous ones to understand the plot. Everything can easily be picked up from one novel. The exceptional thing about this last novel however, is that he has brought together all the different plot lines and characters from previous books, and has clarified and finished them up with no loose ends... a very satisfying ending to an intriguing set of literary thriller books.<br /><br /><i>The memories we bury under mountains of silence are the ones that never stop haunting us.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11995710841166450195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2534889031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2534889031" />
    <a title="Sean Gibson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20955173-sean-gibson"><img alt="Sean Gibson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416866667p2/20955173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2534889031?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Gibson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Gibson" href="/user/show/20955173-sean-gibson">Sean Gibson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062668691" href="/book/show/37677977-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2534889031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1618268762466217403">It’s hard to know exactly what to say about a story that’s about stories that are, in turn, about stories. <br/><br/>Ruiz Zafon’s magical (if occasionally frustrating) Cemetery of Lost Books quadrilogy defies easy categorization. Is it a thriller? Well, it’s certainly suspenseful. A mystery? It’s got unanswered questions in droves, and people trying to tease out answers. A romance? It’s got passion aplenty, and meet-cutes galore. Historical fiction? Intricate details of the Spanish past abound, and Barcel</span>
  <span id="freeText1618268762466217403" style="display:none">It’s hard to know exactly what to say about a story that’s about stories that are, in turn, about stories. <br /><br />Ruiz Zafon’s magical (if occasionally frustrating) Cemetery of Lost Books quadrilogy defies easy categorization. Is it a thriller? Well, it’s certainly suspenseful. A mystery? It’s got unanswered questions in droves, and people trying to tease out answers. A romance? It’s got passion aplenty, and meet-cutes galore. Historical fiction? Intricate details of the Spanish past abound, and Barcelona is as much a character as any human. Literary fiction? The prose (aided in no small part by the brilliant work of translator Lucia Graves) saunters sumptuously across the page, overwritten at times, perhaps (but, when was the last time our most pyrotechnic literary lights were masters of understated style?), but so gorgeously atmospheric that you just want to get lost on it, even if, in so doing, you lose one of the occasionally perplexing plot threads.<br /><br />In short, it’s all of these things, and never more so than in Labyrinth, where Ruiz Zafon brings to a close the twisty story he launched in THE SHADOW OF THE WIND. <br /><br />Whenever someone asks me to recommend a book, I try to ascertain whether they’re the kind of person who likes stories. I don’t mean whether they like stories in the specific sense—clearly, if they’re asking me for a book recommendation, they read, and so they must like some kind of story (I’m less dumb than I sound, I prom…well, I was going to say “I promise,” but that may not be entirely true; is it, however, in this instance)—but rather whether they like stories as an abstract concept. That is, story as idea. As shorthand for a narrative construct wherein anything and everything is possible, and the only thing that matters is how quickly and deeply you can engage with it, how fully realized its world and characters are, and whether, when it concludes, your heart is full and some aspect of the story—a scene, a line, a character, an idea—lingers at the top of your mind for days, or even weeks. If I determine that they are, in fact, the kind of person who likes stories, I invariably recommend SHADOW OF THE WIND.<br /><br />To those same people, if they managed their way through THE ANGEL’S GAME and THE PRISONER OF HEAVEN—both entertaining in their own right, but far less exemplary embodiments of story—I strongly urge you to envelope yourself in LABYRINTH and not only complete the journey, but revel in its intricately intertwined story threads, teased out by a master storyteller at the height of his powers. LABYRINTH is utterly immersive, and whether you love or hate the characters (and if you don’t love the irrepressible Fermin Romero de Torres, you are either 1) dead, in which case I applaud your ability to continue to read, and implore you to teach me your secret; or 2) someone on whose chair I’d very much like to plant a whoopee cushion), you’ll get lost in the twisting, mysterious streets of a Barcelona that simultaneously exists in the past and never existed. <br /><br />Is it a flawless story? By no means. In particular, there is a pervasively misogynistic point of view evinced by numerous male characters that feels jarring, even if it’s not necessarily an inaccurate characterization. But, no story is perfect, nor is any character (except maybe for Sam-I-Am; dude was persistent). This one however, comes close to perfectly embodying what a story should be, and it’s well worth the journey for those willing to give themselves over to it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1618268762466217403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2550651109" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2550651109" />
    <a title="Marialyce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1277371-marialyce"><img alt="Marialyce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601165932p2/1277371.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2550651109?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer15652656392547105373">5 amazingly wonderful stars<br/>My reviews can be seen here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://yayareadslotsofbooks.wordpress.com/'>https://yayareadslotsofbooks.wordpres...</a><br/><br/>This book is the fourth and the last installment of the series that started with The Shadow of the Wind published in 2001 and which went on to be a best seller. Continuing this series was another outstanding book The Angel's Game followed by The Prisoner of Heaven. All of these presented to the reader the underbelly of Barcelona during and after the terror reign of Franco. The characters written of in</span>
  <span id="freeText15652656392547105373" style="display:none">5 amazingly wonderful stars<br />My reviews can be seen here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://yayareadslotsofbooks.wordpress.com/">https://yayareadslotsofbooks.wordpres...</a><br /><br />This book is the fourth and the last installment of the series that started with The Shadow of the Wind published in 2001 and which went on to be a best seller. Continuing this series was another outstanding book The Angel's Game followed by The Prisoner of Heaven. All of these presented to the reader the underbelly of Barcelona during and after the terror reign of Franco. The characters written of include the wonderful young boy, Daniel, who lost his mother at so young an age, the gregarious and wise Fermin, the evil Fumero and a cast of others as they plot murder, and destroy any and all who stand in their path. All the characters of both this book and the others give one a glimpse into not only the times they inhabited, but also a fine and circumspect look into themselves.<br /><br />In this outing a new character is introduced, Alicia. She is the very epitome of a strong woman, battling the forces of evil that had invaded Spain while a dictator held ultimate power. She is a part of the secret police and agrees to one final case to investigate that of the disappearance of Mauricio Valls, the cultural minister of Spain. Aided by her partner, Juan Manuel Vargas, she discovers a hidden book in Valls' desk. This book leads Alicia and others down a path to the horrors of her childhood, the atrocities of the regime, as well as into The Cemetery of Lost Books, which allows her to confront her past. It also brings her into contact with Daniel and the Sempere family and bookstore.<br /><br />This book is at times mystical, there is always present that layer of corruption, that mist inspired look into Barcelona that pushes you forward into a complicated, intricate plot that holds one in as the over eight hundred pages are read. The scenes keep coming at you, holding you enthralled and the dialogue so often witty and humorous, propels you into an affinity with the characters.<br /><br />This is truly a masterpiece, as were all the books in this series. Mr Zafron has been able to weave a story so intricate, so alluring that I felt a bit sad that this journey with Daniel was brought to an end. I most heartily recommend this book, this series for all the reasons we read books. Truly this is true "Reading is dreaming with eyes open." In this book, this author has truly tapped into a world of dreaming, relevance, and treasure.<br /><br />Thanks go out to my local library for providing me with this truly awesome book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer187375781068203877"><s>​This book was too freaking long. </s> This book was freaking amazing and not nearly long enough! <br/><br/>For the first 250 pages or so, I just could not get into this book. I was cursing the author and publisher for such a lengthy book. Too long, too much information. 805 <i>pages</i>?? -- Could we <i>really</i> not edit it down a bit? Would it hurt something to leave out some of the characters' stories or details of their lives? Would the reader curl up and die if a few of the descriptions and back stories were left ou</span>
  <span id="freeText187375781068203877" style="display:none"><s>​This book was too freaking long. </s> This book was freaking amazing and not nearly long enough! <br /><br />For the first 250 pages or so, I just could not get into this book. I was cursing the author and publisher for such a lengthy book. Too long, too much information. 805 <i>pages</i>?? -- Could we <i>really</i> not edit it down a bit? Would it hurt something to leave out some of the characters' stories or details of their lives? Would the reader curl up and die if a few of the descriptions and back stories were left out? Because Zafon's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_" title="The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Wind</a> is one of my all-time favourite novels, I forced myself to keep with this one. Am I ever glad that I did! After about 300 pages, I began getting "into" it though still not loving it. I think if I'd read books 2 and 3 in this series, I wouldn't have had this problem. The author says that one needn't read these in any certain order but I think they should be. <br /><br />Once I got to around 500 pages in though, everything changed and I absolutely LOVED this! Senor Zafon is a <b>GENIUS</b>! I cannot recommend this book, this series, highly enough. This is master storytelling. The character development, the plot, the dialogue, the descriptions -- all SUPERB! It could have been triple the length and yet it still wouldn't be long enough. If you enjoy a brilliantly-written literary novel with suspense, intrigue, murder, you must read this series!</span>

  <span id="freeText3554520835508897614" style="display:none">[<b>4.5 stars</b>] What a bittersweet moment: ending a series you adore, especially the follow up to a book you love with your whole heart. There's no way a book like that can live up to what you've conjured in your mind, but Zafon came close.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3164589682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3164589682" />
    <a title="Anna Luce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9429655-anna-luce"><img alt="Anna Luce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604227738p2/9429655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3164589682?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Luce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Luce" href="/user/show/9429655-anna-luce">Anna Luce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062668691" href="/book/show/37677977-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=7-not-for-me">7-not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=disappointing-reads">disappointing-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=inane-protagonists">inane-protagonists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=2020-reviews">2020-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=covers-i-love">covers-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=skimmed">skimmed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3164589682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11217000498121628390">★★✰✰✰ 2 stars<br/> <br/>From the blatant sexism pouring through each page to its bloated plot, <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> offers an inadequate conclusion to what I considered to be an entertaining series. If anything this disastrous farewell has made me reevaluate the whole Cemetery of Forgotten Books series. I vaguely remember finding the female representation in these books to be somewhat questionable. The women are passive, mere love interests. So, initially I was pretty excited to read <i>The Labyrinth</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11217000498121628390" style="display:none">★★✰✰✰ 2 stars<br /> <br />From the blatant sexism pouring through each page to its bloated plot, <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> offers an inadequate conclusion to what I considered to be an entertaining series. If anything this disastrous farewell has made me reevaluate the whole Cemetery of Forgotten Books series. I vaguely remember finding the female representation in these books to be somewhat questionable. The women are passive, mere love interests. So, initially I was pretty excited to read <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> given that unlike its predecessors it stars a female protagonist...who sadly turns out to be a walking and talking clichè. <br /><br />Like its title suggests, and similarly to the previous books, <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> presents its readers with a labyrinthine storyline. Carlos Ruiz Zafón once again showcases his penchant for melodrama, as well as a fondness for sprinkling Gothic and Romantic elements onto his narrative. There are also many aspects of <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> suggest that Zafón was also influenced by nineteenth-century Sensation and Detective fiction.<br />To begin with I appreciated Zafón's humour, especially since it took the edge off from some of the somber scenes, but by the end I was so irritated by his one-dimensional characters that I was no longer amused by it. That’s when I realised that many of the jokes were made by men at women’s expense. After that things just went downhill. While I may have been intrigued by the baroque structure of his story, amused by some of the more clever pieces of dialogue, and even impressed by certain descriptions, ultimately I just could not stomach the rampant sexism in his novel.<br /><br />One could try to lazily justify Zafón's sexism by arguing that it is ‘historically authentic’....but I’m not sure it is. This novel is hardly realistic or historically accurate. And while the story takes place in 1959, Spain, Zafón uses Victorian ideals of gender in which women fall into either of these categories: they are objects of men’s sexual desire or pure and fragile virgins prone to mysterious maladies. Regardless of the category they fall into—‘whore’ or ‘angel’—their bodies will be objectified.<br />Alicia, one of the central figures in <i>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</i> is considered ‘different’ because she excels at her job as an investigator for Spain’s secret police. She is brusque and manipulative. She is also emotionally and physically scarred...two things that keep her from being wholly independent. Alicia, unlike her male counterparts, mostly gets things done by using the men around her...and it seems that no man can resist her. She is a ‘damaged’ ‘vixen’ who has no qualms about turning men’s attraction towards her to her own advantage. Yet, she often insists on playing solo, landing herself in dangerous or stupid situations. Time and again a man has to help her when her old injury plays up. She has no agency of her own and relies on male characters to help her (all the while claiming that she is a solitary creature). Men are attracted to her not because she is forthright or intelligent but because they are turned on by her ‘promiscuous’ ways. Not only does she openly flirt with them (oh my!) but she’s also a ‘lush’. Male characters with far worse habits are painted in far less judgemental light. All the male characters (all of whom are able-bodied) are incredibly patronising towards her and her body. Rather than calling them out, the narrative makes their behaviour seem a sign of their ‘fatherly’ love for her (most of these father figures also would like to sleep with her).<br />Female characters hate Alicia because they see her as a threat. They are jealous because she’s beautiful and sexy, and they worry that she will take their men. <br />Ultimately, like in the previous books, Alicia becomes a mere object of desire, her whole character reduced to the effect she has on the men around her. While she is presented as ‘subversive’, she is made emotionally and physically ‘unstable’, so that in actuality she can only operate when aided by a man.<br />The other female characters are just as one-dimensional. They either have ‘loose’ morals, and shake their hips to entice men, or are vulnerable because they are too pure for this world. All of the male characters are horny and find any excuse to talk about women’s breasts and thighs. Fermin, a character I used to find ‘funny’, is constantly talking about his sexual desire towards women, and it is usually made into some big joke. More problematic still is Fermin and another male character’s fixation with ‘mulatto girls’ (when talking about cigars one of them says: “They bring them to me straight from Cuba. Sheer class, the sort the mulatto girls roll between their thighs ”). These are the only instances when ‘mulatto’ girls are mentioned...<br />The way Zafón portrays his female characters is not ‘historically accurate’, it is just sexist. Why do his male characters, regardless of whether they fall into the good or bad category, are shown more empathy than his female ones? Alicia is constantly objectified and undermined by the narrative, even in those passages that are from her perspective. Why even bother with this pretence at being ‘subversive’ when in reality you are presenting your readers with the classic ‘damaged woman’?<br />When Zafón's female characters are able to escape dangerous situations on their own they always suffer in a way male characters do not <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[so that they either become so ‘mentally unstable’ that they would commit sucide or they have to endure months of rehabilitation <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Zafón's women exist merely to be desired….and I’m supposed to believe that in the 1950s women did not have any agency at all? That their personalities were near non-existent? Even a novel dating from the Victorian era would present us with a more complex portrayal of female identity…<br /><br />I’ve kept the worst thing about this book for last. Something happens towards the end of this novel that made me hate a character I previously liked.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Daniel, our ‘hero’, rapes his wife. Yep. Here is the scene (tw rape):<br />“At daybreak, when Bea asked him what was wrong, Daniel stared at her but said nothing. Then he undressed her angrily. He took her forcibly without looking her in the face, holding down her arms over her head with one hand and brusquely opening her legs with the other.<br />“Daniel, you’re hurting me. Stop, please. Stop.”<br />He ignored her protests and charged at her with a fury Bea couldn’t remember, until she freed her hands and stuck her nails into his back. ”<br /><br />A few lines later Bea has forgiven him and tells Daniel that: “I’d like to have another child. A girl. Would you like that?”<br /><br />This rape is made to seem as a mere emotional outburst on Daniel’s part. There are no repercussions or guilt, and everything goes back to normal...but after this scene I found it impossible to view Daniel as the hero the narrative was making him to be <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />The story goes on too long, and it ends up being a rather convoluted and overdramatic mess. There are few predictable twists and the ending ruined the whole series: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ turns out that Daniel’s son wrote all of these books...which is yuck given that it means that he wrote a book from his father’s perspective in which he had sex with his mother, and later using a third perspective he wrote a scene in which his father rapes his mother <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />While I can recognise that Zafón is both a terrific wordsmith and a marvellous storyteller, I can't turn a blind eye to how sexist his gargantuan novel is.<br /><br /><a href="https://wishfullyreading.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Read more reviews on my blog</a> / / / <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/9429655-anna-luce" rel="nofollow noopener">View all my reviews on Goodreads</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11217000498121628390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1758932482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1758932482" />
    <a title="Gabrielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle"><img alt="Gabrielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598976963p2/6753400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1758932482?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabrielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabrielle" href="/user/show/6753400-gabrielle">Gabrielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42243497-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=ouch-my-feels">ouch-my-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=ereader">ereader</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1758932482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12287238733398654505">Carlos Ruiz Zafon’s “The Shadow of the Wind” is arguably my favourite book (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226430093);'>https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> I have multiple editions, and every time I see it at a used bookstore, I buy it and give it to someone because the sight of this book alone on a shelf makes me want to find it a good and loving home. Every time a new installment of the Cemetery of Forgotten Books series came out, I ran to the bookstore to get a copy and locked myself in to devour it. To say that my expectations an</span>
  <span id="freeText12287238733398654505" style="display:none">Carlos Ruiz Zafon’s “The Shadow of the Wind” is arguably my favourite book (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226430093);">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> I have multiple editions, and every time I see it at a used bookstore, I buy it and give it to someone because the sight of this book alone on a shelf makes me want to find it a good and loving home. Every time a new installment of the Cemetery of Forgotten Books series came out, I ran to the bookstore to get a copy and locked myself in to devour it. To say that my expectations and excitement were high for “The Labyrinth of Spirits” would be an understatement; this is the final part of the story, the book that brings this beautiful neo-Gothic saga full circle, and it feels like I had waited years (seven, to be exact) to find out how the story ends.<br /><br />From the very first page, I was immediately sucked in that lovely, familiar atmosphere: Zafon’s beloved Barcelona and its beautiful buildings, enveloped in mist and mystery. I was reunited with sweet Daniel Sempere and the incomparable Fermin Romero de Torres, but I also made a new friend with the enigmatic Alicia Gris. A survivor of the Mussolini bombings, she is a gifted investigator whose life is inextricably linked to Daniel and Fermin’s stories: she is assigned to solve the disappearance of Minister Mauricio Valls, a case in which her most important clue is a strange book – part of an extremely rare series known as “The Labyrinth of Spirits”. In the course of her investigation, she will unearth many secrets about a couple of doomed writers who were prisoners at the Montjuic Castle during the war, and how their stories deeply affected the lives of a small family of book-sellers...<br /><br />Alicia is a fascinating protagonist: Zafon has not written a tough female characters before (Isabella in “The Angel’s Game” being the notable exception), and I was happy to find Alicia to be strong, smart, flawed and complicated. I loved her sharp observations, her tough character and her interactions with Vargas. Alicia sees the world with more lucidity than most people, and while she is reckless and manipulative when it comes to getting the job done, her hardened exterior shields her many wounds.<br /><br />All of Zafon’s characters have suffered a cruel loss, and have been changed by their grief. “The Labyrinth of Spirits” digs deeper than the other books of the series into how the Civil War essentially took a wrecking ball through people’s lives, and how surviving the aftermath of such an event put everyone in a situation where good people can turn bad very easily. His stories-within-stories are beautifully convoluted, but not confusing: they illustrate the world contained within each character perfectly, and how intimately connected each story is to the other.<br /><br />I saw some reviews that mentioned not liking the final part, "The Book of Julian", and I can see why, as it tries to bring a bit of reality into Zafon's mist-shrouded Neo-Gothic world, but I liked it. I like to think it's a bit autobiographical... I personally thought this was the perfect conclusion to what very well may be my favorite series of books.<br /><br />Zafon’s novels are love letters to books, to the magic of reading and its power to change your life. His prose is absolutely exquisite, and his gift as a storyteller, capable of spinning a gorgeous and intricate yarn, which makes this 800-page book feel like it was over much too soon. If you have enjoyed the previous books of the Cemetery of Forgotten Books series, do not miss this one. If you love books, darkly seductive stories, beautiful but haunting images seared in your brain, and if you can take having your heart broken by a good book, read it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12287238733398654505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2844651648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2844651648" />
    <a title="Andrew Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith"><img alt="Andrew Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605605555p2/5885760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2844651648?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Smith" href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith">Andrew Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40363213-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5885760-andrew-smith?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2844651648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6539532482901877405">I <i>suppose</i> you could read this novel as a standalone piece, and the same could be said of the other three books in this series. But to me that just doesn’t make sense. Equally nonsensical to me is the author’s assertion that the books can be read in any order. Really? I’ve read many series in random order and sometimes that works just fine but occasionally you come across one that relies quite heavily on a pre-knowledge of prior events or of characters who have graced the pages in an earlier epis</span>
  <span id="freeText6539532482901877405" style="display:none">I <i>suppose</i> you could read this novel as a standalone piece, and the same could be said of the other three books in this series. But to me that just doesn’t make sense. Equally nonsensical to me is the author’s assertion that the books can be read in any order. Really? I’ve read many series in random order and sometimes that works just fine but occasionally you come across one that relies quite heavily on a pre-knowledge of prior events or of characters who have graced the pages in an earlier episode and whose back story you are totally oblivious. This can really compromise enjoyment of the tale you’re currently immersed in. And I think that this is very much the case here. So unless you’ve already dipped your toe into the tales of <i>The Cemetery of Forgotten Books</i>, do yourself a favour and start at the beginning and work your way through. You might want to take some notes too, because there are a lot of characters and many linkages you’ll need to keep track of. Do this and I believe you’re in for an absolute treat!<br /><br />The stories cover a period spanning 1919 – 1992 and at the core is the Sempere family who run a bookshop in Barcelona. It’s hard to pin down which genre you’d place the books in – they seem to embrace fantasy, mystery, magical realism, historical fiction and crime fiction too. There’s certainly a good sprinkling of Spanish history here, particularly in the focus on the banning and the burning of books and the missing children of the Franco years. The time frame is jumpy and this doesn’t make it any easier to keep a clear track of events, but this also gives the overall tale width and depth. A sense of not quite knowing what’s going on becomes the norm. The characters are engaging and range from the angelic to the completely repulsive. It’s dark most of the time, particularly in this last book.<br /><br />For the record, this final chapter focusses on a new character called Alicia Gris who is employed by the Secret Police to track down the missing Culture Minister, Don Mauricio Valls. Reader of the earlier books will know that Valls is a self-serving egomaniac and that, in truth, the world would be better place were he to be permanently removed from it. Alicia is joined by a partner who has been foisted upon her, called Vargas, and together they dive deep into the murky underworld of Barcelona. The chemistry between the two is expertly developed and I quickly found immensely enjoying their interactions. The plotting is clever too, as I’d grown to expect, and overall the story is told in a way that is both charming and completely captivating. I won’t go into the detail of the book other than to say that all loose ends are tied off here and – if you’ve been paying attention throughout the series – it all ultimately makes sense. <br /><br />If I have a bone to pick it would be that the language (translated from the author’s native Spanish) is sometimes a little flowery and maybe some scenes are a little protracted. But if that’s my only complaint in over 800 pages here, and in 2000 plus pages across the the four books, then I feel that I’m possibly being a little picky. It really is a magnificent body of work. The stories are big enough to block out the world around you as you slip deep into the world Zafon has created and full of characters who become more, much more, than just names in the pages of a book. A poetic, gothic masterpiece of gargantuan proportions. I’m just sad I’ve reached the end of it.<br /><br />My sincere thanks to Orion Publishing Group and NetGalley for providing a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6539532482901877405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2532856706" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2532856706" />
    <a title="Lou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45941903-lou"><img alt="Lou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517829400p2/45941903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2532856706?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lou" href="/user/show/45941903-lou">Lou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781474606189" href="/book/show/39099067-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2532856706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9094174784292767272">'The Labyrinth of the Spirits' is the fourth and final installment in the Cemetery of Forgotten Books series. I don't mind telling the world that this happens to be one of my favourite series of all time, and Carlos Ruiz Zafon is very much criminally underrated in my view. Having loved the previous three books, I was hoping to be completely blown away once again by Zafon's superb storytelling ability. It's safe to say he didn't let me down, and this lived up to my incredibly high expectations. O</span>
  <span id="freeText9094174784292767272" style="display:none">'The Labyrinth of the Spirits' is the fourth and final installment in the Cemetery of Forgotten Books series. I don't mind telling the world that this happens to be one of my favourite series of all time, and Carlos Ruiz Zafon is very much criminally underrated in my view. Having loved the previous three books, I was hoping to be completely blown away once again by Zafon's superb storytelling ability. It's safe to say he didn't let me down, and this lived up to my incredibly high expectations. One thing I would say is that although this is stated as working as a standalone, I feel you will be landing in the middle of the action with no clue what is happening, and you'll miss out on the all important background information from previous books which I feel is required in order to completely immerse yourself in the story.<br /><br />At 832 pages in length, this is a rather daunting prospect when you first open the book. I thought to myself that so long as the writing is as exquisite as ever, I would have no problem with the page count. As always, Zafon is expert at grabbing the readers attention and pulling them into the story, and because of this it actually felt a lot shorter than it actually was. It's a complex and intricate novel that requires your full attention, but boy are you rewarded highly! Essentially, this is a story about the insufferable and traumatic barbarism of Spain's fascist past. An enchanting and haunting tale written by one of the most talented writers of the fiction world. If you're a fantasy/historical/mystery fan this is well worth your time. I am really sad that this is the end of the series, but it was certainly a fitting conclusion. Unmissable. I look forward to Zafon publishing more of his work.<br /><br />Many thanks to W&amp;N for an ARC. I was not required to post a review, and all thoughts and opinions expressed are my own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9094174784292767272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3359031803" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3359031803" />
    <a title="Royce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551187-royce"><img alt="Royce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603816088p2/4551187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3359031803?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Royce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Royce" href="/user/show/4551187-royce">Royce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781443457132" href="/book/show/37954156-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551187-royce?shelf=best-books-of-all-time">best-books-of-all-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3359031803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12053450887117902434">Instant masterpiece. Reading <i>The Cemetery of Forgotten Books</i> is just like putting a jigsaw puzzle together--the more you read, the more you get a whole new perspective on the lives of the characters. Passionate leading and supporting characters that are all equally meticulous and obsessed with literature. Even the setting itself--Barcelona, <i>beautiful and gloomy</i>, is just as majestic as any of the characters in the series. Perfect gothic environment.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2580358158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2580358158" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/911560-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533239415p2/911560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2580358158?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/911560-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/911560-christine?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/911560-christine?shelf=stuff-i-think-of-as-good-fiction">stuff-i-think-of-as-good-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/911560-christine?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/911560-christine?shelf=terrific-mainstream">terrific-mainstream</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2580358158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15185984532064132566">I love this book, but let me tell you what it isn't. The three previous novels in this series all had a gothic feel that made the mysteries in their pages feel personal in scope. Despite the backdrop of Franco's Spain, the true backdrop was a house or a shop. The third installment, The Prisoner of Heaven, gave us a foreshadowing of the shift from place to regime, but kept the focus on Fermin. <br/><br/>In this final installment, those mysterious places still exist but they are overshadowed by the regime. </span>
  <span id="freeText15185984532064132566" style="display:none">I love this book, but let me tell you what it isn't. The three previous novels in this series all had a gothic feel that made the mysteries in their pages feel personal in scope. Despite the backdrop of Franco's Spain, the true backdrop was a house or a shop. The third installment, The Prisoner of Heaven, gave us a foreshadowing of the shift from place to regime, but kept the focus on Fermin. <br /><br />In this final installment, those mysterious places still exist but they are overshadowed by the regime. This change leads to a much less gothic mystery and delves more deeply into the actual price of the war and Franco regime on the individual. <br /><br />Ruiz Zafón has recreated a world where no one can be trusted. The central mystery of Valls' disappearance is quickly overwhelmed by the mysteries uncovered by Alicia Gris, an agent of the secret police. Valls becomes a side note in a world of spiders, both figurative and literal, that destroy everything in their paths. Unfortunately, I felt the stories of Alicia and her partner Vargas were cut short in order to put the focus back on the Sempere family. <br /><br />But who can complain when young Julian Sempere gets lines like, "what Fermin says is that wise men own up when they sometimes make mistakes, but idiots always make mistakes, even though they never admit it and always think they're right. He calls it his Archimedean Principle of Communicable Imbecilities."<br /><br />But even with changes, we get some of the gothic, and some of that "mystery" of books, such as when Alicia discovers the National Library in Madrid and finds it to be her safe space. And different doesn't mean bad. The Labyrinth of the Spirits is an amazing work in its own right and one well worth your time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15185984532064132566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
