    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2524697665" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2524697665" />
    <a title="Artemis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15999633-artemis"><img alt="Artemis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525212496p2/15999633.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2524697665?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Artemis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Artemis" href="/user/show/15999633-artemis">Artemis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781474606189" href="/book/show/39099067-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15999633-artemis?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15999633-artemis?shelf=geek-culture">geek-culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15999633-artemis?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15999633-artemis?shelf=sequels">sequels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15999633-artemis?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15999633-artemis?shelf=mysticism-of-life">mysticism-of-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15999633-artemis?shelf=about-writing">about-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15999633-artemis?shelf=gritty">gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15999633-artemis?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15999633-artemis?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2524697665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer419982963411378293">Content warning: sexual assault.<br/><br/><br/><br/>No.<br/><br/>What in the seven circles of Barcelona was that?<br/><br/>Throughout reading 'The Labyrinth of the Spirits', the most-anticipated, final book of the brilliant, breathtaking 'The Cemetery of Forgotten Books' series, I was intrigued by the characters, but mostly I was bored by the slow pacing and quite frankly mundane events stringing along a rather dull mystery plot. <br/><br/>I tried to care, I really did, but maybe it had been too long since I'd read the previous book in the seri</span>
  <span id="freeText419982963411378293" style="display:none">Content warning: sexual assault.<br /><br /><br /><br />No.<br /><br />What in the seven circles of Barcelona was that?<br /><br />Throughout reading 'The Labyrinth of the Spirits', the most-anticipated, final book of the brilliant, breathtaking 'The Cemetery of Forgotten Books' series, I was intrigued by the characters, but mostly I was bored by the slow pacing and quite frankly mundane events stringing along a rather dull mystery plot. <br /><br />I tried to care, I really did, but maybe it had been too long since I'd read the previous book in the series, 'The Prisoner of Heaven'. Or, tragically, had the magic lost its spark? Had the enchanting writing gone and run its course? Yeah, even the writing wasn't that engaging and masterful (helped by the usually fantastic translation job). It was just "okay".<br /><br />However, I trudged on, on the quest to care, and near the end of 'The Labyrinth of the Spirits', it did start to pick up for me. More time is spent with the old, familiar characters, and the spirit of 'The Shadow of the Wind' was rising once again. Things were looking up, and paying off.<br /><br />But then, at about eighty pages left of the book, something truly horrendous and unforgivable happens. Committed by the main character of these books no less. It comes right out of nowhere and is forgotten just as quickly. The shock of it was like a whiplash to the brain and soul; a smack in the face to all who had read and loved the previous books. In the narration it is a small but evil act that I will not let pass, nor allow to be excused, no matter how little the author thinks of it.<br /><br />What is the event that killed the book for me?<br /><br />Final content warning: sexual assault.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Daniel tries to rape Bea. Right out of the blue, he pushes her on the bed, forcibly undresses her, and assaults her, all through her protests. She actually has to dig her nails into his back in order to push him off her with all of her strength. Let me reiterate: The main character, whom you are supposed to care for, sympathize with and follow, to see him achieve his goal of a happy life, attempts to rape his wife. Oh sure, he's been left traumatized by a revelation about his deceased mother, Isabella - a revelation that anyone who has read 'The Angel's Game' would have figured out, and yet this book, after 700 pages of "buildup", treats it like it's the plot twist of the century. Uh, no. It's painfully obvious to anyone who knows anything about stories and tropes. Why did you have to go down that predicable, fanfiction-y path, Zafón? It doesn't even mean anything in the end. <br /><br />But anyway, Daniel is sad and the ever-patient and understanding Bea is right there and he gets... frustrated, I guess, to put it extremely lightly. Frustrated at life? At women? Is it meant to show him giving in to his base, animal instincts, after a human truth dealt him a blow? His way of taking his shock - that turns his world upside down and changes his perspective - out on someone whom he "loves" most? Who knows and who gives a shit: nothing excuses rape. Nothing. Even factoring in the book's time period being set before marital rape was considered a thing, and therefore not illegal. It is still a fucking awful, evil and out-of-character moment for Daniel. <br /><br />Oh, but don't expect there to be any consequences for his actions, oh no. Bea is angry at him... for two pages, and then they have consensual sex, after which she talks about having a second child with him. The attempted rape is never mentioned again. <br /><br />WHAT. THE. HEAVENLY. FUCK!? <br /><br />The same day her husband sexually assaulted her she wants to have more of his babies! And Bea is usually an intelligent, down-to-earth character who is very much involved in Daniel's tumultuous life. He doesn't even apologise to her; he thinks about it, but doesn't actually say anything to her, because talking to women, specifically your supposedly-beloved significant other, is so hard, yo. So much easier to just rape them.<br /><br />Don't worry, they'll forgive you and let it slide. And you don't have to say anything or do anything to earn that forgiveness.<br /><br />Daniel doesn't need to carry on with his plan of revenge and murder in order to become a monster. He had already shown his true colours beforehand. As a repressed misogynist.<br /><br />I am so fucking sick of seeing attempted rapists being excused and even lauded as heroes in fiction. And in real life. Fuck that shit. It's 2018 - we desperately need to do better.<br /><br />Daniel Sempere is dead to me. As is this series and its highly questionable attitude towards women. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Even without that Moral Event Horizon moment near the end, which would have caused me to rage-quit if I didn't force myself to persevere the last hundred pages of this 800-page bore, other things annoyed me about 'The Labyrinth of the Spirits'. <br /><br />Like the leading lady, a new character named Alicia Gris, a gothic callback to the femme fatale in film noir. Alicia is a great detective struggling through a painful hip, inflicted when she was a child in the second world war. I liked her - a not-big but still remarkable improvement on the series' female representation, in that she does save herself from men from time to time, and she has a real, complex personality: a wide array of feelings, flaws, and a determination to see justice done, regardless of anything else. Except that every single male in the book is in love with her, or is infatuated with her, or is at least enticed by her mysterious, gothic, red lipstick air. This leads to every single female in the book to absolutely despise her. Like, serious hatred. <br /><br />*sigh*. Historical fiction or not, I'm sick of seeing this normalization of Victorian gender dynamics (men are base creatures (heterosexual, of course) who are unable to keep it in their pants, internalized misogyny, etc.) in YA books, so adult books such as this have no excuse.<br /><br />Not helping matters is Alicia deliberately encouraging these men's arousal upon laying eyes on her; sometimes for favours, sometimes because she's just lonely. She seems to kiss guys at random. I'm not slut shaming her, I'm only disappointed because it hinders her image as a strong independent adult woman, who braved hell and back to get where she is.<br /><br />Good political commentary aside - as in, rich and powerful men are the worst; the true plague on human society - I was still fairly bored with 'The Labyrinth of the Spirits'. For such a long novel, it's infuriatingly anti-climatic, not that the mystery element was ever that exciting to begin with. Too many characters, too many over-describing of places - sometimes even of places we've already been introduced to - and the new, less interesting characters are spotlighted at the expense of old characters. Fermin is still a laugh, though, when he does show up.<br /><br />Yet another disappointing read this year. I'm sick of it. I'm sick of being disappointed by hyped books. I'm sick of being disappointed by sequels to my favourite books. 2018 truly is the year of disappointments. The year of "Who gives a fuck anymore?"<br /><br />Frack 2018.<br /><br />We have to do better. We have to. We must we must we must.<br /><br />With that, I'm out. Hope you have a better day than me.<br /><br />Final Score: 2/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="419982963411378293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2687900888" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2687900888" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2687900888?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/37561508-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2687900888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3210855025637423242"><strong><em>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</em> is one of the best books I've ever read. It has it all - evocative history, engrossing mystery, atmospheric setting, compelling characters, incredible emotional depth - wrapped up in writing so beautiful that it moves your soul.</strong><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"Stories have no beginning and no end, only doors through which one may enter them."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br/>I finished reading this book earlier last week and before I had the opportunity to pen my review in praise of such magnificence, I was shocked by t</span>
  <span id="freeText3210855025637423242" style="display:none"><strong><em>The Labyrinth of the Spirits</em> is one of the best books I've ever read. It has it all - evocative history, engrossing mystery, atmospheric setting, compelling characters, incredible emotional depth - wrapped up in writing so beautiful that it moves your soul.</strong><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"Stories have no beginning and no end, only doors through which one may enter them."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />I finished reading this book earlier last week and before I had the opportunity to pen my review in praise of such magnificence, I was shocked by the news of Carlos Ruiz Zafón's passing. With just this quartet, Zafón became one of my favourite authors, and The Cemetery of Forgotten one of my all-time favourite series. I was so affected by his passing which occurred so soon after I've finished the last book he has written; and what a masterpiece it was. The world has truly lost an incredible talent and is now duller with his absence.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"A labyrinth of shimmering forms ascended towards an immense glass dome. Moonlight, split into a thousand blades, poured down from up high and threw into relief the seemingly impossible geometry of a spell made of up all the books, all the stories, and all the dreams in the world."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />In my review for <i>The Prisoner of Heaven</i>, I've mentioned that interconnected narrative threads were starting to come together for the characters we've met since the first book. In this final book, these labyrinthian threads come together in a magnificent tapestry that told an incredibly engrossing and moving story. A story about the intertwined lives of these people, of how they were affected by the Spanish Civil War and the regime under General Franco, and of how books and its stories indelibly impact their lives, both readers and writers. Presenting the narrative in the form of both a mystery and thriller set in an atmospheric historical setting was a stroke of brilliance, which was realised with Zafón's masterful storytelling and exceptional writing.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>
    <blockquote>"People live inside their hopes, but the landlord of fate is the devil."</blockquote>
  </strong>
</em><br />The binding threads throughout the series were The Sempere &amp; Sons bookshop (and by extension, the Sempere family) and the Cemetery of Forgotten Books. Daniel and his father, his wife, Beatriz and Fermìn continue to feature heavily in the final book as the story traverses back in time for a while to the Civil War. The story introduced a new main character here, Alicia Gris, an orphan survivor of the war which left her partially broken and in constant pain. Her characterisation was almost as spellbinding as that of David Martìn's. There's something inexplicably captivating about broken and tragic characters, and Alicia was definitely one of those. As the story comes to a close here, I will refrain from mentioning more. What I will say is that the closure was brilliantly executed. While the author mentioned that the books could be read in any order, I'd strongly suggest to follow the publication sequence for maximum impact.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"This is where tragedies and romances began and ended, as did escapes and returns, betrayals and absences. Life, some said, is a railway station where one almost always enters, or get put into, the wrong carriage."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />The entire series gave me one of the most emotionally charged reading experiences I've ever had, but Zafón truly saved the best for last. My heart ached so much that it was sore and tender by the time I finished the book. However, it was not all sorrow and grief, and because of the rarity of such reprieve, those beautiful and touching moments no matter how small were rendered ever more precious. I also could not deny the allure of books about books, and the magical quality of books and stories that permeated through these was positively enchanting.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>“The memories we bury under mountains of silence are the ones that never stop haunting us.”</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />Speaking of being enchanted, I have to talk about the beauty of the prose again. Zafón's writing and Graves' translation seemed to work magic on the emotions of the reader. To me, beautiful prose is not about being flowery or purple, but writing that emotes and speaks to one's soul. There's a musical quality to it that worked in cadences and tones to convey the heart and soul of the story. And even though I've not read many classics yet, I think that Zafón had achieved for post-Civil War Spain what Dickens had done for Victorian England. His writing, however, was more attuned to the modern reader with the added appeal of bibliophilia as a central theme.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"Tell our stories to the world, and never forget that we exist so long as someone remembers us."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />With storytelling almost as perfect as it could be, <i>The Cemetery of Forgotten Books</i> was simply too memorable to be forgotten. Highly, <i>highly</i> recommended to all readers.<br /><br /><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Labyrinth-Spirits-Carlos-Ruiz-Zafon/9780062668707/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u> | <u><a href="https://bookshop.org/books/the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits/9780062668691" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookshop.org (Support Independent Bookstores)</a></u></b> | <u>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.amazon.co.uk/gp/product/B07DCY1MX1" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a>
  </b>
</u> | <u>
  <b>
    <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Labyrinth-Spirits-Carlos-Ruiz-Zafon/dp/0062668706" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a>
  </b>
</u><br /><br /><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-1WG" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and my other reviews at <a href="http://novelnotions.net/category/book-reviews/tss-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions.</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3210855025637423242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1825446958" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1825446958" />
    <a title="Juan Quibrera" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31394270-juan-quibrera"><img alt="Juan Quibrera" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588873030p2/31394270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1825446958?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juan Quibrera" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juan Quibrera" href="/user/show/31394270-juan-quibrera">Juan Quibrera</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1825446958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9264633292068521578">Mmmmm I got mixed feelings for this one. I love Carlos Ruiz Zafon, his writing and -most of all- his characters. The Shadow of the Wind is, still today, one of my all-time faves. However, this concluding novel felt...well, uneven. Some of it was brilliant, some of it was extremely corny, albeit very nostalgic. The plot (for the biggest chunk of the book) was quite convoluted and -in my opinion- contrived. There were far too many characters and a lot of filler scenes. And the book was just unnece</span>
  <span id="freeText9264633292068521578" style="display:none">Mmmmm I got mixed feelings for this one. I love Carlos Ruiz Zafon, his writing and -most of all- his characters. The Shadow of the Wind is, still today, one of my all-time faves. However, this concluding novel felt...well, uneven. Some of it was brilliant, some of it was extremely corny, albeit very nostalgic. The plot (for the biggest chunk of the book) was quite convoluted and -in my opinion- contrived. There were far too many characters and a lot of filler scenes. And the book was just unnecessarily long. I still loved the ending, though, and I admit that putting an end to this series is not easy for me. Even though I found this to be the weakest book in the quartet and not one I intend to re-read, it was mostly enjoyable and had some tearing-up moments. Bravo, Zafon. Great universe, wonderful work. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9264633292068521578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1764040320" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1764040320" />
    <a title="Beatrix" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4763999-beatrix"><img alt="Beatrix" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434973672p2/4763999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1764040320?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrix" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrix" href="/user/show/4763999-beatrix">Beatrix</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789532668759" href="/book/show/35555483-labirint-duhova">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=books-i-ll-never-forget">books-i-ll-never-forget</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=inspiring">inspiring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=cultural">cultural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=beautiful-writing">beautiful-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=strong-females">strong-females</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1764040320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16763110613466669276"><i>(see English review below) </i><br/><br/>Lavirint duhova je još jedno remek djelo gosp. Safona, koje je mnogo mračnije i komplikovanije od svih prethodnih knjiga ovog serijala. S obzirom da kada je prvi dio napisan ova knjiga nije bila planirana, Safon je odlično uklopio sve dijelove. Lavirint duhova povezuje i objašnjava prethodne tri knjige, ali i ima posebnu priču.<br/><br/>Radnja se dešava 1959. i počinje u Madridu gdje upoznajemo nove likove, no nekih 200ak stranica kasnije radnja se premješta u Barselonu. Najznač</span>
  <span id="freeText16763110613466669276" style="display:none"><i>(see English review below) </i><br><br>Lavirint duhova je još jedno remek djelo gosp. Safona, koje je mnogo mračnije i komplikovanije od svih prethodnih knjiga ovog serijala. S obzirom da kada je prvi dio napisan ova knjiga nije bila planirana, Safon je odlično uklopio sve dijelove. Lavirint duhova povezuje i objašnjava prethodne tri knjige, ali i ima posebnu priču.<br><br>Radnja se dešava 1959. i počinje u Madridu gdje upoznajemo nove likove, no nekih 200ak stranica kasnije radnja se premješta u Barselonu. Najznačajniji novi lik je Alisa Gris. I po meni ona je ženski lik koji je falio u prethodnim Safonovim djelima – ona je snažna, samostalna žena koja se snalazi u tom okrutnom “muškom” svijetu. Alisa nije lik koji će prijati svima, okrutna, sarkastična, ovisnica; no meni se jako svidjela, ima tu neku mračnu auru i volim takve likove za koje ne znaš da li su baš dobri ili zli.<br><br>I sam ton romana je drugačiji od prethodnih, odrasliji, mračniji i po prvi put jedan žanr prevladava više od drugih – krimić. <br><br>Sva četiri romana iz serijala su na mojoj polici absolutnih favorite i imaju moje najveće preporuke. Safon čarobno piše i ovim knjigama ću se sigurno vraćati iznova i iznova.<br><br>***<br>Thank you, Mr. Zafon, for giving us another masterpiece! <br><br>(There were two things I wanted while reading this saga <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[for David and Isabella to be together; and to get a book about Julian Sempere <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and in this novel, I did in a way get my wish fulfilled.)<br><br>This particular installment is darker, gloomier and more complicated than previous books. For the first time the story centers around a murder-mystery. We meet new characters, of whom Alicia is my favorite. She is the type of female character that was missing in previous Zafon’s books – strong, independent woman who is equal with men in “their” world. I loved her!<br><br>After reading the last page, I was left feeling both happy and sad. It was like saying goodbye to old friends. And while I understand it was time to finish the series, there is no more story to tell here, I do hope Zafon continues with some spin-off maybe? New characters but same setting and time period? <br><br>Overall, I enjoyed this novel immensely and all four books of the series are among my all time favorites! I can’t recommend them enough.<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_" title="The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1344545047s/1232.jpg" alt="The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5196764.The_Angel_s_Game__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___2_" title="The Angel's Game (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #2) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1434302581s/5196764.jpg" alt="The Angel's Game (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #2) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13623012.The_Prisoner_of_Heaven__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___3_" title="The Prisoner of Heaven (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #3) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1335994402s/13623012.jpg" alt="The Prisoner of Heaven (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #3) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>Zafon is my #1 favorite author, his writing is magical, I love the setting (Barcelona, 20th century), he combines genres (mystery, historical, romance, etc.), but above all his novels are about books – his love towards literature. He creates a world in which books are worth killing for, where characters go to extreme lengths to protect books, and where books truly impact and change the lives of his characters. And such a world is truly an incredible place.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16763110613466669276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788711537572" href="/book/show/39277754-ndernes-labyrint">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2327128504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15572652603085822173">I wanted to love this book more than I actually did.<br/><br/>It's not that it wasn't good. Or page-turning. Or unbearably deceptive. It was, as Zafón's books always are. In fact, it was perhaps too familiar. It repeated not only itself, but the entire series, constantly underlining its overused metaphors.<br/><br/>And it was too long. Something I thought I'd never write about a Zafón novel, but it really was. While it was never boring reading it, the story sometimes strayed a bit too far from its focus.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2893130135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2893130135" />
    <a title="Catherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57588338-catherine"><img alt="Catherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596467036p2/57588338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2893130135?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine" href="/user/show/57588338-catherine">Catherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/50828917-the-labyrinth-of-the-spirits">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57588338-catherine?shelf=thriller-and-mystery">thriller-and-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57588338-catherine?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2893130135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4636296970031861385">1) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2893126558' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shadow of the Wind</a> ★★★★★<br/>2) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2893129810' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Angel's Game</a> ★★★★☆<br/>3) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2893129978' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Prisoner of Heaven</a> ★★★☆☆<br/><br/><i>"Stories have no beginning and no end, only doors through which one may enter them."</i><br/><br/>I have a new favorite book series. While the third book did disappoint, the last novel of The Cemetery of Forgotten Books went back to being amazing. Yes, the first book is the best, I won't argue with anyone about that, but I also loved the second and fourth books. The author has an incredible talent and created a story, a uni</span>
  <span id="freeText4636296970031861385" style="display:none">1) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2893126558" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Wind</a> ★★★★★<br />2) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2893129810" rel="nofollow noopener">The Angel's Game</a> ★★★★☆<br />3) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2893129978" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prisoner of Heaven</a> ★★★☆☆<br /><br /><i>"Stories have no beginning and no end, only doors through which one may enter them."</i><br /><br />I have a new favorite book series. While the third book did disappoint, the last novel of The Cemetery of Forgotten Books went back to being amazing. Yes, the first book is the best, I won't argue with anyone about that, but I also loved the second and fourth books. The author has an incredible talent and created a story, a universe and characters that truly are unforgettable. It's the kind of book series that you don't want to see ending, that leaves you thinking about those novels instead of picking another book right after, the kind of book series I already know I'll read again.<br /><br />This final installment has much less of a gothic vibe, which could have been disappointing for me as it was one of my favorite part of those books, but the plot and subplots are clever as always, the language is still beautiful, the historical part takes more place without being too confusing for those who don't know Spain History too much (I think so, at least, since I'm far from considering myself a specialist), and we still have the magic of books inside this book. I also loved the new character, Alicia, and the humor was just great.<br /><br />My personal thoughts on how much I loved those four books: The Shadow of the Wind is the best, then The Angel's Game, then The Labyrinth of the Spirits and finally The Angel's Game. While the author said, if I remember well, that each book could be read as a standalone, I highly recommend to read them in order. It's just a beautiful and magical experience that you don't want to miss, and while I understand that each novel could be considered as a standalone that doesn't required having read the previous books, it doesn't quite makes sense to me at the same time. I don't think it's a good idea to read them in any order, but it's only my personal opinion. I cannot possibly comment on the quality of the translation, so I'll leave this to those who could read the series in Spanish.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4636296970031861385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GEgRglyJ2iHjJFNO6JGBm8BNJ8eFquqX0qDcyV4neTKS1pYojXteYEdZbCTrZPaI0ajaaY8h5tXYM8A3768HWQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pvrG8gAu/Zlc5UxnQOK4znH7LHO8ReWEZFc89j1iH/UsZEFY0dx52PiYcw1DF8/dYB7R3bbO6cZuxCAIjOphng==')})
  }

Among them is Roser, a pregnant young widow, who finds her life intertwined with that of Victor Dalmau, an army doctor and the brother of her deceased love. In order to survive, the two must unite in a marriage neither of them desires.\n\nTogether with two thousand other refugees, they embark on the SS Winnipeg, a ship chartered by the poet Pablo Neruda, to Chile: “the long petal of sea and wine and snow.” As unlikely partners, they embrace exile as the rest of Europe erupts in world war. But they will also find joy as they patiently await the day when they will be exiles no more. Through it all, their hope of returning to Spain keeps them going. Destined to witness the battle between freedom and repression as it plays out across the world, Roser and Victor will find that home might have been closer than they thought all along.\n\n\n  A Pero el reverso de tanta nobleza es la tendencia de los señores de la torre a padecer el trastorno de identidad múltiple, un detalle que arrastrará a Estíbaliz a vivir una arriesgada historia de amor. \n\nUnai López de Ayala acabará descubriendo que Los señores del tiempo tiene mucho que ver con su propio pasado. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16663669349994029923">Carlos Ruiz Zafón was a Spanish novelist. Born in Barcelona in 1964, he lived in Los Ángeles, United States, since 1994, and worked as a scriptwriter aside from writing novels.<br/><br/>His first novel, <i>El príncipe de la niebla</i> (<i>The Prince of Mist</i>, 1993), earned the Edebé literary prize for young adult fiction. He is also the author of three more young-adult novels, <i>El palacio de la medianoche</i> (1994), <i>Las l</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16663669349994029923" style="display:none">Carlos Ruiz Zafón was a Spanish novelist. Born in Barcelona in 1964, he lived in Los Ángeles, United States, since 1994, and worked as a scriptwriter aside from writing novels.<br /><br />His first novel, <i>El príncipe de la niebla</i> (<i>The Prince of Mist</i>, 1993), earned the Edebé literary prize for young adult fiction. He is also the author of three more young-adult novels, <i>El palacio de la medianoche</i> (1994), <i>Las luces de septiembre</i> (1995) and <i>Marina</i> (1999).<br /><br />In 2001 he published the novel <i>La sombra del viento</i> (<i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>), his first 'adult' novel, which has sold millions of copies worldwide. Since its publication, <i>La sombra del viento</i> has garnered critical acclaim around the world and has won numerous international awards. Ruiz Zafón's works have been published in more than 40 countries and have been translated into more than 30 languages.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16663669349994029923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

  <!--
This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
